## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics: nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The variables x (position), v (velocity), t (time), and dv_dt (acceleration) match a second-order ODE of an oscillator written in first-order form, where dv_dt is modeled as a combination of restoring forces, damping/friction, and possible external/parametric forcing. Nonlinear harmonic oscillators commonly express dv_dt as functions of x, v, and sometimes explicit time dependence.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Free particle / constant acceleration: dv_dt = c0 (baseline acceleration or bias term)
- Linear spring (simple harmonic oscillator): dv_dt = c0 * x (Hooke-like restoring acceleration; sign absorbed into c0)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (drag proportional to velocity; sign absorbed into c0)
- Damped harmonic oscillator (linear): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (mass-normalized spring + damper model)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator (nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillation via state-dependent damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * v**2) * v (negative damping at small |v|, positive at large |v|)
- Liénard-type oscillator (generalized): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x + c3 * x**2) * v (broad class including many relaxation oscillators)
- Dry friction / Coulomb-like damping (smoothed): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (velocity sign-dependent friction with smoothing)
- Quadratic drag: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like drag in 1D motion)
- Externally driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (periodic forcing)
- Multi-harmonic forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (richer periodic excitation)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear parametric stiffness: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * x**3 + c4 * v (parametric drive with Duffing nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: conservative oscillators often have dv_dt as an odd function of x (e.g., c0*x + c1*x**3), producing symmetric phase portraits about the origin.
- Energy-conserving vs dissipative: if dv_dt depends only on x (no v, no t), the system is closer to conservative; adding v terms introduces dissipation or self-excitation.
- Viscous damping signature: a term linear in v (c*v) yields exponential decay of amplitude in the underdamped regime when combined with linear restoring force.
- Limit-cycle indicator: state-dependent damping such as (c0 + c1*x**2)*v or (c0 + c1*v**2)*v typically produces self-sustained oscillations with an attracting periodic orbit.
- Hardening/softening stiffness: adding x**3 (Duffing) causes amplitude-dependent frequency; the sign of the cubic coefficient controls hardening vs softening behavior.
- Dry friction signature: tanh(c*v) or sign-like terms create stick-slip tendencies, flatter velocity near zero, and non-sinusoidal oscillations.
- Aerodynamic drag signature: v*Abs(v) introduces stronger damping at high speed and can distort waveform asymmetrically in time (faster deceleration at peaks of |v|).
- External forcing fingerprint: explicit sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms imply entrainment, resonance peaks, and steady-state oscillations even with damping.
- Parametric resonance fingerprint: coefficients multiplying x that vary periodically in t (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) can produce instability tongues and rapid amplitude growth near 2:1-type conditions.

-0.0230405406738805\,v^3\;-\;1.1056075693807\,x\,(0.0552411020531317|v|^{1/3}+1)\;-\;1.1056075693807\,x\;+\;0.350781823399691\sin t
\]
Combine the two linear-in-\(x\) pieces:
\[
= (-0.0230405406738805)\,v^3\;+\;(-1.1056075693807\cdot 0.0552411020531317)\,x|v|^{1/3}\;+\;(-2.2112151387614)\,x\;+\;0.350781823399691\sin t
\]
So GT is exactly of the form
\[
A\,v^3 + B\,x|v|^{1/3} + C\,x + D\,\sin t
\]
with fixed constants \(A,B,C,D\) (and **no** other dependence on \(x,t,v\); in particular no logs/exp/ratios, no extra \(v\) terms, no constants offset).

Also, any candidate using \(\cos(t+\phi)\) can match \(D\sin t\) by choosing \(\phi=\pi/2\) and scaling amplitude/sign appropriately since \(\cos(t+\pi/2)=-\sin t\).

Now check candidates:
